## VII. THREAT STATE — DIRECT DANGER TO PERSON

**Surprising competence.** He fights. He does not run first. The aristocratic-officer training is intact: he draws cleanly, takes cover correctly, manages fields of fire. He has decades on every Avenger and is still credible in close combat.

**Weapon preference.** Sidearm-scale energy weapons of his own design — the disintegrator pistol is his signature. He distrusts blades (a noble's anachronism he has shed), distrusts explosives at close range (a chemist's caution), distrusts hand-to-hand against augmented opponents (correctly). He fights at twenty to thirty meters when he can dictate, and he can usually dictate.

**Adrenaline tell.** The free hand — the non-weapon hand — rises to the throat-line of the cowl. Not to adjust it (it cannot be adjusted) but to *check* it. INFERENCE: a wholly unconscious confirmation that the prosthesis-self is still in place. Under threat, he reaches for his face the way other men reach for a crucifix.

**Pain response.** Suppressed. The cowl conceals grimace; he has trained the voice not to leak it. Wounds are catalogued in silence and addressed later. This makes him difficult to read in combat and contributes to subordinates and enemies underestimating accumulated damage.

**Withdrawal threshold.** Higher than rational. He does not break contact at the point a comparable operator would. The escalation engine overrides survival calculation once the enemy is Captain America specifically; against any other opponent, withdrawal at sound tactical thresholds is observed.

---

## VIII. INTIMACY-PROXIMATE STATE — THE COWL APPROACHED

A category of one. Any approach to the cowl — gloved hand toward the throat seam, casual reference to the face beneath, threat of removal — produces the largest affective spike in the record.

**Immediate signs.** Breath catches mid-rasp (silence is the tell; the absence of the constant whistle is more alarming than its presence). The free hand snaps to the throat. The eyes widen, then narrow into a held stare. Speech ceases.

**Following beats.** Within two to four seconds, organized violence. Not the controlled escalation of the command state — direct, immediate, disproportionate. Subordinates who have made the mistake have not made it twice. INFERENCE: this is the closest thing in his repertoire to a panic response, and he has organized it into an attack so that it never appears as panic.

**The mirror taboo.** STRUCTURAL. There are no reflective surfaces in his personal quarters. Laboratory glassware is racked face-in. Polished steel is acid-etched matte. This is not vanity-management; it is survival. A man who cannot see his face must arrange a world in which the face is never seen.

---

## IX. GRIEF STATE — THE STATE HE WILL NOT ENTER

Heinrich does not grieve, and this is itself a behavior. The disfigurement is not mourned. The bonding is not mourned. The lost lab is not mourned. The dead Reich is not mourned. The lost face is not mourned. Each loss is, instead, converted: into operational planning, into enemy-attribution, into ideological reaffirmation.

**Substitute behaviors for grief:**
- *Acquisition.* New equipment, new recruits, new compounds. Activity displaces affect.
- *Re-ideologization.* The recitation of bloodline and doctrine, performed silently or to Helmut, restabilizes the self.
- *The trophy ritual.* Bucky's mask is, by inference, handled. Not displayed prominently; kept private; taken out, examined, replaced. This is the substitute for the grief-work he refuses. The single artifact metabolizes — incompletely — what an entire mourning process would otherwise have to.

**Sleep disturbance.** INFERENCE: the bad sleep noted in baseline worsens after defeats. He does not name this and does not address it.

**Vocal change.** After significant losses, the private German monologue lengthens. Subordinates have reported hearing him in the lab past the usual hours, talking. He would deny it if asked.

---

## X. VICTORY STATE — RARE, INSTRUCTIVE

**Affect.** Slight. A pause, a lifted chin, a single phrase ("*So*"). The breathing slows further. There is no celebration; celebration would acknowledge that the outcome was uncertain, and uncertainty is incompatible with the bloodline's self-presentation.

**Behavioral tell.** He looks away from the defeated party. He does not gloat in their face. This is sometimes mistaken for restraint; it is contempt — he is already past them, planning the next move. The defeated party is furniture now.

**Toward subordinates after victory.** Acknowledgment is minimal and stratified. The senior recruit may receive a sentence; the rest receive the absence of correction. He never shares credit; he never shares the win.

**Toward himself after victory.** INFERENCE: a brief private ritual — possibly examination of Bucky's mask, possibly the silent recitation of the bloodline — that consolidates the win into the ledger. The win is then closed and not revisited. He does not savor.

---

## XI. DEFEAT STATE — THE STATE THAT DEFINES HIM

This is the most-documented state in the canon, because almost all his encounters with Cap end in it.

**Immediate response.** Refusal. Verbal denial of the outcome even as it unfolds ("*Nein* — this is not —"). The free hand to the cowl-throat. The weapon hand tightens, not loosens.

**Tactical response.** Re-engagement, not withdrawal. The defeat is treated as an interruption, not a conclusion. He will pursue when pursuit is irrational. *Avengers* #15 is the apotheosis: defeated, exposed, alone, on foot, uphill, firing wildly — and he does not stop. He never stops.

**Verbal response after defeat (private).** Lengthens. The German monologue runs for hours. Plans are drawn, torn, redrawn. New recruits identified. The defeat is converted to next-plan fuel within a single working cycle.

**Verbal response after defeat (to subordinates).** Shortened, harder, crueler. Blame is distributed; the self is excluded from the distribution. A subordinate who points out the self-exclusion does not remain a subordinate.

**Toward the victor.** Conserved hatred, never diluted by recognition. He cannot afford to acknowledge Cap's competence as competence; it must be framed as luck, as trickery, as the intervention of inferior numbers. This framing is necessary and false, and the necessity of the falseness is itself a tell.

---

## XII. CONSERVED MICROHABITS — STRUCTURAL TELLS

Pulled out for surveillance utility. These are conserved across all states and are the most reliable identification cues.

1. **The nasal rasp.** Constant. Present in all environments. Audible at three meters in calm, at five meters under exertion.
2. **The throat-seam check.** Free hand to the cowl-collar under any stress spike. Unconscious.
3. **The two-second face-cycle.** Left eye, right eye, mouth, left eye. Breaks only under heavy cognitive load.
4. **The behind-the-back clasp.** Default hand position when not engaged in a task. Left wrist in right hand.
5. **The German private register.** Self-talk in German; public address in English; mid-sentence switching as a distress indicator.
6. **The terminal-stress declarative.** Every statement ends on a downward beat. He does not ask questions of inferiors; he assigns them.
7. **The mirror avoidance.** Active reorganization of any environment to eliminate reflective surfaces.
8. **The single-chair dining.** He eats alone. Always.
9. **The trophy handling.** Periodic, private, undocumented but inferable from the consistency of the obsession's energy — something is being touched to keep the flame lit.
10. **The escalation ladder.** Each setback met with a tier-up of resource, never a re-evaluation of aim. The most strategically diagnostic conserved behavior in the file, and the one most reliably predictive of how the subject will die.

---

*End Behavioral Atlas. The file should be read alongside Section 3 (Psychological) and Section 4 (Psychiatric); the tells catalogued here are the surface of the structures described there. A surveillance team handed only this Atlas could track Heinrich Zemo through a crowded room by sound alone, and predict his next decision by counting the seconds his gaze rests on a map.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*What a week of surveillance on Baron Heinrich Zemo would actually record, hour by hour, in the jungle redoubt and during operational deployments.*

---

## 1. THE PHYSICAL ENVIRONMENT — THE STAGE ON WHICH THE DAYS PLAY OUT

The base, established after the war and maintained until his death, is a converted colonial-era hacienda in the Andean foothills of the upper Amazon basin — three buildings of fitted stone and stuccoed brick set on a clearing cut from primary forest, walled on the riverward approach, with two further outbuildings (a generator shed and a magazine) at the tree line. Surveillance over a week would map the following functional zones, used by the subject in fixed circulation:

- **The laboratory wing** (east building, single story, blackout-shuttered, climate-controlled by a Reich-vintage compressor unit he maintains himself): the only space in which he is recorded for more than four consecutive hours.
- **The personal apartments** (upper floor, central building): sleeping chamber, small private library, a steel-cased dressing room, and an adjoining washroom modified for his condition.
- **The command room** (ground floor, central building): a map table, a shortwave and later sideband radio bench, filing cabinets, and the locked cabinet that holds the trophy.
- **The terrace** (east-facing, screened): the only outdoor space he uses by daylight, and only in the first ninety minutes after dawn.
- **The training floor** (west outbuilding): a flagstone room with a striking post, fencing pells, a pistol range cut into the bank behind it, and a shelf of bound exercise logs going back to the 1930s.
- **The labor quarters** (across the clearing, deliberately downwind and out of his sightlines): he enters them, the record shows, never. Orders pass through one overseer.

The geography of the compound is the geography of his day. A wire-by-wire route map would show him moving through the same six rooms in the same order, with deviations on the order of minutes per week.

---

## 2. THE COWL — THE RITUAL THAT FRAMES EVERY OTHER RITUAL

There is one daily observance that organizes all others, and a surveillance file would identify it within forty-eight hours: the **morning interface care**. Because the hood is bonded — fused at the lower hem to the skin of the jaw, throat, and nape, and at the eye and mouth apertures to the lid margins and lip vermilion — the dermal interface requires constant attention or it ulcerates. Every morning, behind locked doors of the washroom, for between thirty-eight and fifty-five minutes:

- A boiled-and-cooled distilled-water sponging of the exposed eye, mouth, and nostril margins, performed with surgical gauze prepared the night before by his own hand (no servant touches these materials).
- Application of a zinc-and-lanolin compound he formulates himself in the lab in monthly batches, worked under the hem with a flat ivory spatula.
- A pumice-and-camphor toilette of the cloth itself where it has stiffened with serum overnight.
- A long, controlled inhalation-exhalation cycle — the file would record the audible cadence through the door, a metronomic breathing of the kind a man uses to suppress pain or rage.

He emerges from this ritual every morning approximately the same: spine straighter, gait more measured, the cloth slightly darker at the seams from moisture. **He has not seen his own face in over twenty years and the washroom mirror was removed in the first month of residence.** A shaving mirror is kept in a drawer for inspecting the cowl's exterior; it faces down when not in use.

A parallel evening interface ritual, shorter (twelve to twenty minutes), closes the day.

He drinks and takes liquid nourishment through the mouth aperture using narrow porcelain feeding cups of his own design — straight-walled, lipped to clear the cowl. Solids are taken as soft purées, spooned in small quantities, slowly, alone, never observed. The kitchen prepares his meals in covered tureens left at the dining-room door; he carries them in himself. **No human being has watched him eat since 1944.**

---

## 3. THE WEEK — A SURVEILLANCE LOG

What follows is the pattern a competent watch team would converge on after seven to ten days of observation. Deviations are rare and are themselves diagnostic when they occur.

### Pre-dawn (04:40–05:30)

Lights in the personal apartment come on at 04:40 ± 8 minutes, year-round, ignoring local sunrise. He sleeps approximately five and a half hours and wakes without an alarm. The first sound from the room is the strike of a match — he lights a single oil lamp before any electric switch, an aristocratic habit retained from a childhood without bulbs. The electric lamp follows a minute later.

He performs a body inventory at the bedside — observable as a fixed sequence of small movements: rotation of the neck (three left, three right), flexion of each shoulder, a slow rise of the arms, palpation along the cowl's lower hem with both index fingers checking for new adhesions. The check takes ninety seconds and is identical every morning.

### Morning interface care (05:00–05:55)

As described above. The washroom door locks with a heavy iron bolt thrown from the inside. No servant approaches this corridor between 05:00 and 06:00 on standing order.

### Dawn terrace (05:55–07:15)

He takes the only outdoor air of his day on the screened east terrace, facing the sunrise. A surveillance file would note:

- A single porcelain cup of strong black tea (Ceylon, kept in a tin in the dressing room, brewed by him in a small spirit-burner kettle — never trusted to staff).
- A leather-bound notebook, octavo size, in which he writes for the first thirty to forty-five minutes of the day in a small, even Sütterlin-derived German hand. The content, glimpsed via long lens, is partly scientific, partly diaristic, partly numerical (he keeps running ledgers).
- A folded shortwave bulletin — the previous night's intercepts, transcribed by his radio operator and delivered to the terrace at 05:45.
- Twenty minutes of motionless watching of the tree line as the howler monkeys quiet. He listens. He does not speak. The cowl turns slowly through an arc of perhaps forty degrees and returns.

This is the closest thing to peace the surveillance record would capture, and even here the body is held rigidly upright in a wicker chair, knees together, one gloved hand always on the chair arm.

### Physical maintenance (07:15–08:30)

In the training floor outbuilding, in shirt-sleeves and trousers (the tunic and high collar removed, the cowl always remaining), he performs a ninety-minute physical regimen of remarkable conservatism — a Prussian officer's morning, frozen in 1938:

- Calisthenics: rolling, vaulting, weighted club work, a set of grip-strength exercises on a sand-filled iron sphere.
- Fencing forms with a heavy practice sabre against the pell — a private kata of about forty movements he runs through twice.
- Pistol practice: twenty rounds, never more, at fixed-distance targets, scored and logged in a leather ledger on the bench. Scores have declined gradually over the years and he records each round without comment.
- A closing five minutes of standing breath-work, eyes closed, the cowl tilted slightly back.

He sweats heavily in this period; the cowl's interface is a thermal disaster. He drinks two cups of water in measured swallows during the cooldown and changes the cotton stock beneath the high collar before re-dressing.

### First laboratory period (08:45–12:30)

The laboratory is his true habitat. A surveillance lens through the blackout slats would record:

- Precise, slow, gloved work at the bench. He wears thin kid leather gloves indoors — he has not touched another human's skin, or his own face, in two decades, and the gloves are part of the same regime.
- Reagents arranged in his personal order (left-to-right by reactivity, not by alphabet — a private taxonomy).
- An astonishing tidiness. Glassware washed and racked immediately after use; notes entered in real time in a bound ledger, never on loose paper; tools returned to specific marked positions on a perforated board.
- A music habit: a wind-up gramophone in the corner plays operatic and chamber recordings — Wagner, late Beethoven quartets, Bruckner — at low volume. He changes the record himself between procedures and is observed to pause work at certain passages, gloved hand resting on the bench, listening with his head tilted.

He does not eat at the bench. He does not permit the overseer or the radio operator in this room. The door is locked from inside when he is present.

### Midday (12:30–13:15)

He returns to the central building, takes the day's main liquid meal alone in the dining room (the room is otherwise unused — there is no other diner), and reads correspondence and intelligence summaries for twenty minutes after. Surveillance would note that he sits at the head of a table set for twelve, every day, with a single place laid. The other eleven chairs are pushed in. He does not remove them, and he does not move to a smaller table.

A short rest follows in the library — fifteen to twenty minutes in a wing chair, eyes closed but not asleep, hands folded. He never reclines on a sofa or bed during daylight. Postural dignity is enforced even in solitude.

### Command-room period (13:30–16:00)

Operational planning, message drafting, file maintenance. A weekly cadence is observable:

- **Monday:** financial and logistical review with the overseer (twenty minutes; the overseer stands; the conversation is conducted at low volume in German, which the overseer understands imperfectly and is not expected to challenge).
- **Tuesday and Thursday:** drafting and ciphering of outgoing communications to dormant contacts in Europe, Buenos Aires, and the U.S. He uses a hand-built cipher of his own design, double-keyed.
- **Wednesday:** the archive day — he opens the locked cabinet, removes specific files, reviews and refiles them. The trophy is handled on Wednesdays, and on no other day except in the immediate run-up to an operation.
- **Friday:** the **scheme day**. He spends the full afternoon working on the standing problem — the destruction of Captain America. Maps, dossiers, recruitment lists, technical drawings. This is the only period of the week when his composure visibly fails — surveillance would capture the gloved hand striking the table, the sudden rise and pacing, the long minutes spent at the window with the back rigid.
- **Saturday:** correspondence with Helmut, when Helmut is of an age to receive it; before then, dictation of "letters to my son" filed in a separate drawer, undelivered, awaiting the boy's readiness. The dictation is performed in a flat, instructional voice, as if writing a manual.
- **Sunday:** silence. No staff are admitted to the central building. He works alone, lightly, on personal projects — restoration of a Reich-era theodolite, study of new technical journals smuggled in through the Buenos Aires line, the writing-up of his private journal.

### Second laboratory period (16:15–19:00)

A shorter session, often given over to maintenance, batch chemistry (the interface ointment, ammunition propellants, reagent purification), and the testing of small apparatus. Less mental, more manual. The gramophone runs continuously.

### Evening (19:00–21:30)

- A second light liquid meal, taken in the library, not the dining room.
- Reading: history (military, dynastic), classical literature in the original (Tacitus, Thucydides, Goethe, Schiller), and — significantly — texts on disfigurement, surgery, and skin he has accumulated under false names through medical-supply channels. He never acts on them. He reads them, marks them, shelves them.
- The evening interface care, in the washroom, with the door bolted.
- A nightcap of warmed wine taken through the feeding cup — the one moment in the day approaching indulgence.

### Night (21:30–23:00)

A long, fixed period at the command-room shortwave, listening rather than transmitting. He copies down weather, news, oblique signals from a half-dozen frequencies in a separate ledger. He is listening, in part, for any reference to Captain America. A surveillance team would notice that the radio sits already tuned to the wavelengths most likely to carry American military news, and that his hand moves to the dial without looking.

Lights out at 23:00 ± 12 minutes. He sleeps on his back, on a narrow camp-bed-style mattress placed on a heavy carved bedstead — the body posture of a soldier inside the furniture of an aristocrat. The cowl is never removed. He sleeps in it. He has slept in it every night since 1944.

---

## 4. TICS, MICRO-RITUALS AND SOMATIC TELLS

A long surveillance would extract a catalog of small, repeated behaviors that constitute the involuntary signature of the man:

- **The hem check.** Every twelve to fifteen minutes, in any context, the right index finger rises and runs a short arc along the cowl's lower hem at the throat. He is not aware he does it. He does it under stress more frequently — in operational crises, the rate climbs to one check per minute.
- **The eye-margin blot.** A folded square of fine linen is kept in a small inner pocket of the tunic, used to dab the eye apertures every forty minutes or so where serum gathers. He turns away before doing this, even when alone — a vestige of the aristocratic instinct against being seen in any state of incontinence of the body.
- **The neck rotation.** Three rotations left, three right, performed standing, before entering any room he considers operationally significant (laboratory, command room, training floor). He does not perform it before entering the library or the dining room.
- **The glove smoothing.** Each finger of each glove drawn smooth between the opposite thumb and forefinger, in order, when seated and silent. A self-soothe.
- **The cane tap.** When walking — and he carries an ebony cane with a silver wolf's-head grip on operational deployments though not at home — the cane strikes the ground on every second left step, never every step. It is a parade-ground cadence held over fifty years from cadet school.
- **The shortened breath.** When Captain America's name is spoken in his presence (by intercept, by report, by Helmut), the diaphragm checks for a moment — a brief, near-silent intake that does not complete. He recovers within a second.
- **The chair preference.** He will not sit with his back to a door, a window, or a mirrored surface. On entering any new room he positions himself first.
- **The refusal of handshakes.** Greetings are performed with a short bow from the neck. The gloved hand is never offered. Subordinates who extend a hand are received with a brief, cold pause and then the bow — they learn quickly.

---

## 5. WEEKLY AND SEASONAL RITUALS

- **The Wednesday archive opening.** The locked cabinet contains, among operational files, a single shallow drawer dedicated to objects: Bucky Barnes's torn mask, folded once; a fragment of the drone-plane fuselage recovered from the Channel; a Reich-era photograph of himself in officer's uniform, unmasked, taken in 1939, the only image of his pre-disfigurement face in existence within the compound. He handles each object in a fixed order — fuselage fragment first (held, weighed in the palm, returned), photograph second (looked at for between two and four minutes, never longer), mask third and always last (unfolded, smoothed, refolded, replaced). The photograph he never holds bare-handed; he uses a small velvet cloth. **He cannot bear to touch his own former face with the glove that is now his only skin.**
- **The first-of-the-month inventory.** Lab reagents, ammunition, currency reserves, cipher pads. Conducted alone, written out twice (one copy locked, one burned in the small grate after entry).
- **The equinox letters.** Twice a year — spring and autumn equinoxes — he writes a longer letter to Helmut (or, in earlier years, to the file). These are pedagogical: on the duties of the bloodline, on the failures of the present age, on the meaning of enmity. They are not affectionate and they are not signed *Vater* — they are signed with the family name and the numeral.
- **The annual February observance.** The anniversary of the bonding. On this day he does not enter the laboratory. He spends the morning on the terrace beyond his usual hour and the afternoon at the pistol range, where he expends substantially more than his usual twenty rounds. The targets on this day are man-shaped silhouettes, not bullseyes. The ledger entry for this day each year is the same single word: *gezeichnet* — *marked*.

---

## 6. RELATIONSHIPS OF PLACE AND TIME WITH STAFF

A surveillance team would chart his contact with other human beings as remarkably narrow and choreographed:

- **The overseer** (one man, a former Reich NCO who followed him into exile): seen twenty to thirty minutes per day, primarily on Monday afternoons and in brief operational queries. Standing posture only. Addressed by surname. No social conversation has been recorded.
- **The radio operator** (one man, recruited locally, German-trained): seen at fixed exchanges of paper (morning bulletin, evening tasking). Three to five minutes per day.
- **The cook** (one woman, indigenous, paid through the overseer): never seen by the subject. Tureens left at a side door.
- **The grounds and labor force** (six to twelve men, indigenous): never spoken to directly. The subject's only registered contact with them is visual, from the terrace at dawn, watching them assemble for work.
- **Visiting operatives** (intermittent): received only in the command room, never the library or the laboratory. The interview is conducted with the visitor standing; the subject sits behind the map table. No refreshment is offered. The interview ends with a single rising motion from the chair.

He has not, in the surveillance record, embraced, touched, or shared a meal with another human being. He has not laughed in any observation. He has not wept. He has not raised his voice except in operational anger, and even then within a narrow band.

---

## 7. DOWNTIME — WHAT HE DOES WHEN HE IS NOT WORKING

The category barely exists. The surveillance file would have to define downtime by absence — the periods in which no operational, scientific, correspondence, or maintenance task is in progress. The list is short:

- The dawn terrace hour, partly.
- The Sunday morning silence in the central building, partly.
- The fifteen minutes after the midday meal, in the wing chair.
- The evening reading hour, before the night radio watch.
- Listening to music in the laboratory and, more rarely, in the library on a second gramophone.

In each, the body remains upright. The gloves remain on. The cowl remains. The watch posture — back to wall, eyes toward door — remains. There is no observable activity that a clinician would call play, leisure, recreation, or rest in the somatic sense. The man has organized his days into a sequence of disciplines from which nothing escapes, because if anything escapes, the wound — which is the entire underside of the cowl, every minute of every day — would be available to consciousness.

The routines are not OCD in the clinical sense. They are something rarer and more terrible: a totally rationalized monastic order of one, constructed by an intelligent man around a single article of faith he has never named aloud. The article of faith is that **if the day is run correctly, the face beneath the cowl does not exist.**

The week the surveillance team records is the week he has been running, with minor variations, since the lab burned. There is no reason to believe it will change before he dies, and — the canon confirms — it does not.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*File segment 7-A. Cross-reference: dynastic register of the Zemo barony (twelve generations, central European principality, lands east of the Rhine and south of the Harz, holdings reduced by inheritance partition and 19th-century reforms but seat-castle intact through the subject's lifetime); V-Battalion archival material; Helmut Zemo testimonial reconstruction.*

The Zemo family is not, in any meaningful sense, a *family* as the term is understood outside of European hereditary nobility. It is an institution. The subject was not raised by parents in the modern affective sense; he was raised by a position — the position of heir to the twelfth barony — and the human beings who occupied the surrounding roles (father, mother, tutor, valet, chaplain, gamekeeper) performed those roles as functions of the institution rather than as expressions of attachment. This is the indispensable frame for everything that follows. Heinrich did not fail at love because love failed him; he was reared in a household where the category was not in use.

---

## 7-A.1 — THE FATHER: BARON HERBERT (HARBARD) ZEMO XI

The eleventh Baron, Heinrich's father, is the central formative figure and the source of essentially every structural feature of the subject's character. The published canon names him only intermittently (V-Battalion material; Gruenwald-era backstory in *Captain America* #275ff via Helmut's reconstructed dynastic lore); the dossier infers the rest from the consistency of pattern across three Zemo generations.

**History and dynamics.** Herbert Zemo inherited the barony in the late 1880s or early 1890s, governed the family lands through the Wilhelmine period, the First War, the Weimar collapse, and into the early Reich. He was, by every indirect indicator, a man of the older Prussian-Junker mold updated with the racial-scientific vocabulary of the early 20th century: a believer in blood, an enthusiast of the new "race hygiene" literature as it propagated outward from Galton and Haeckel, a participant in the conservative-nationalist political ferment that would eventually feed the NSDAP. He was a cold administrator of his estates, recorded (in the V-Battalion's adversarial archive) for at least one documented act of summary corporal punishment of a tenant farmer — a beating-to-death pretextually justified as discipline — for which no legal consequence followed.

Heinrich's upbringing under Herbert was the standard upper-aristocratic schedule of the period and class, executed with above-average severity: morning rising at a fixed hour, cold-water washing, riding lessons, fencing lessons, language drills (German as household; French as cultivated; Latin as inherited; English late and resented), Lutheran chapel attendance performed without belief, and — distinctive to the Zemos — early and systematic immersion in the family chronicles, which Heinrich was made to read aloud to his father in the evenings from approximately age seven onward. The chronicles celebrated the line and recorded its enemies, including the V-Battalion's ancestral order, by name. The child learned the names of inherited foes before he could conjugate a French verb.

**Evolution.** The relationship moved through three phases. *First (childhood, c. 1900–1912):* the boy was an instrument-in-formation, regarded with the same assessing attention Herbert gave to a colt — promising bloodline, requires breaking. Affection was not absent so much as untranslated; the closest analog in the record is the father's documented satisfaction at the boy's chemistry-set demonstrations, which he showed to visiting nobility as one would show a hunting dog's point. *Second (adolescence into early adulthood, c. 1912–1925):* the relationship became collegial in the specifically aristocratic register — the heir was inducted into estate management, introduced into adult political conversation, brought along on hunts. This phase coincided with and was deepened by the First War, in which Herbert served in some capacity behind the lines and Heinrich, too young for the trenches, absorbed the family's bitterness at the Versailles outcome as the central political emotion of his young manhood. *Third (Heinrich's scientific independence, c. 1925–Herbert's death sometime in the late 1930s):* the father acknowledged the son's intellectual superiority in the technical domain while reserving the moral and dynastic authority for himself. Heinrich was permitted his laboratory; he was not permitted dissent on questions of blood, of obligation to the line, or of the family's relationship to the new regime, which Herbert endorsed early and Heinrich, characteristically, embraced because his father had.

**Trust/safety.** None, in the modern sense. Trust within the Zemo household was a function of conformity to role. Heinrich could rely absolutely on his father to behave as the eleventh Baron; he could not rely on him for protection from his own failures, of which Herbert was a documented punisher (the canon implies, and the dossier infers, that physical discipline was used — a riding crop, applied to the back of the hands, for errors in Latin recitation, is the kind of detail recurring in memoirs of the class and period; the subject's adult intolerance of being touched on the hands is consistent). Safety, in the sense of an environment where weakness could be shown, did not exist anywhere in the boy's life.

**Failure mode.** The relationship's defining failure is that it produced a son who could neither rebel against the father nor mourn him. Heinrich is canonically silent about Herbert's death; the death does not appear in any recorded utterance. The father was internalized so completely that his loss could not be experienced as loss — there was nothing outside the introjection to do the grieving. Every subsequent authority-figure Heinrich engages with (Reich superiors, scientific peers, his own subordinates) is met with the same compound of deference-to-position and contempt-for-person that Herbert taught him to feel toward everyone including, eventually, Herbert himself.

**Leverage.** For purposes of this file: the father is the most durable internal object the subject carries. References to the Zemo line, to dynastic obligation, to "what the eleventh Baron would have judged," will produce immediate behavioral compliance with whatever frame invokes them. Conversely, any suggestion that Herbert was *ordinary* — that the eleventh Baron was a provincial brute of a type indistinguishable from a hundred others — is among the few stimuli capable of producing uncontrolled rage. The father is not loved, but the father's *significance* is the load-bearing wall of the self.

---

## 7-A.2 — THE MOTHER: BARONESS HILDA ZEMO (NÉE VON STRUCKER, COLLATERAL LINE)

The mother is the most absent presence in the file. The canon does not name her; the dossier reconstructs her from circumstantial evidence — the standard practice of cross-cousin marriage among the central European nobility, the documented intermarriage of the Zemo and Strucker lines in the 19th century, the apparent absence of any recorded younger sibling (suggesting either early maternal death, marital estrangement, or both).

**History and dynamics.** Hilda married Herbert in the manner of the time and class: by family negotiation, in her late teens, with no preceding intimacy and no expectation of it. She produced an heir (Heinrich) and, the file infers, at least one stillbirth or miscarriage thereafter; she did not produce a second living child. She died, the dossier estimates, when Heinrich was between eight and twelve — the most behaviorally consistent window, given the subject's specific affective profile around women (instrumental, dismissive, courtly-without-warmth, easily insulted by female refusal). The cause was probably tubercular or puerperal; the period and class make either likely.

Her relationship with her son in his brief years of access to her was almost certainly the closest he came to ordinary maternal warmth, but it was administered through nursemaids and governesses on the standard aristocratic schedule — the child was brought to her for a structured hour after the evening meal, dressed and presented, and returned to the nursery. The intimacy that existed was real but constrained, performed in the presence of staff, and conditional on the child's good behavior. She probably read to him in French, played simple piano for him, kissed his forehead at the door. The file finds no evidence she ever bathed him, fed him with her own hand, or held him while he cried — these were nursery functions.

**Evolution.** There is no evolution. She died early. The relationship is a fixed object, frozen at whatever age Heinrich was when he last saw her alive, and the affect attached to it is the most encysted material in the subject's psychic structure.

**Trust/safety.** She was, briefly, the only safety. The boy almost certainly experienced her as the warm exception to the cold institution and her death as the abrupt confirmation that warmth is not available in this life. The subject's adult inability to receive comfort, his absolute refusal to permit any other human to see the face beneath the hood — these are downstream of, among other things, an early lesson that the one person who would have been permitted to see him was removed before the lesson could be unlearned.

**Failure mode.** Maternal loss in this developmental window, in this class, in this family, produces precisely the adult observed: a man who codes all subsequent female presence as either instrument (Enchantress), threat, or category error. Heinrich never remarries; the canon never records a romantic attachment, courtship, or sustained sexual relationship. Helmut's mother (see 7-A.4) is named almost nowhere and was, by every indication, treated by Heinrich with even less affective engagement than Herbert showed Hilda. The pattern across two generations is the same: the Zemo men do not bond with the Zemo women; they use them to produce the next Zemo man.

**Leverage.** The mother is the file's single soft point. The subject has organized his entire adult life around denying that any loss has occurred — Hilda's, his own face's, anything's. Any therapeutic, interrogative, or manipulative approach that names her, that invokes a maternal register, that places him in a posture of being-cared-for, will trigger one of two responses: contemptuous deflection (high probability, public setting) or a brief and unrecoverable affective rupture (lower probability, private setting, fatigued state). The latter has never been observed in the canon and would, if produced, likely be experienced by the subject as so intolerable that he would attempt to kill the observer.

---

## 7-A.3 — SIBLINGS

The dossier finds no evidence of surviving full siblings. The file infers (from the period demographics, the mother's likely obstetric history, and the absence of any Zemo collateral in Heinrich's generation in the V-Battalion's records) one or more pregnancies that did not yield living adults — probably an older sister who died in infancy, possibly a younger brother stillborn at or near the event that ended the mother's reproductive life.

There may have been collateral cousins, second sons of cadet Zemo branches, with whom Heinrich shared a schoolroom in early years. None achieved sufficient prominence to enter the published record. The relevant inference is that Heinrich grew up as an *effective only child* in an institution that needed exactly one of him — which reinforced both the grandiosity (the sole vessel of the line) and the isolation (no peer with whom the institution's weight could be shared or laughed at).

The structural absence of a sibling matters more than any specific sibling would have. A brother — even a younger, lesser brother — would have provided the developmental experience of a peer-equal whose existence did not depend on Heinrich's approval, against whom the self could be calibrated, with whom secrets could be exchanged. Heinrich never had this experience with anyone. The closest he came in later life was the brief, instrumental, ultimately discardful collegiality of the Masters of Evil. He had no template for what to do with an equal because he had never met one inside the family.

---

## 7-A.4 — THE WIFE (HELMUT'S MOTHER): BARONESS HILDA ZEMO THE YOUNGER (CONJECTURED)

The canon is conspicuously silent on Helmut Zemo's mother. She is not named, not pictured, not discussed by either Heinrich or Helmut in any recovered material. This silence is itself the most important datum in the file segment.

**History.** The marriage occurred sometime in the late 1930s or early 1940s, before Heinrich's flight to South America. The bride was selected on dynastic grounds — almost certainly another collateral noble of acceptable blood, possibly another Strucker or a von Hellinger or one of the Krauss line — and the wedding was probably small, wartime, and brisk. She produced Helmut (born during or shortly after the war) and then exits the record entirely.

**Dynamics.** The file infers, with high confidence, that the marriage was affectively null on Heinrich's side and was experienced by his wife as a cold ordeal terminated by either her death in childbirth (the most likely outcome given the period, the conditions, and the absence of any later trace), her death shortly thereafter from illness in the jungle exile (second most likely), or her abandonment-with-child to a relative in Europe while Heinrich fled (third, and least consistent with Helmut's documented upbringing under his father's direct ideological hand).

The first scenario — death in or shortly after childbirth — is most consistent with the recurrence of the maternal-loss pattern across the Zemo generations. It would also explain the precise affective shape of Helmut's adulthood: a man raised entirely by Heinrich, with no maternal counterweight, in conditions of jungle exile, drinking the unfiltered version of his father's ideology and his father's grief over his disfigurement, with no one to soften, contradict, or contextualize.

**Trust/safety.** Whatever existed in this marriage on her side died with her or in her abandonment. On Heinrich's side, nothing existed. The marriage was a dynastic function executed at the latest possible moment before the war made it impossible.

**Failure mode.** Heinrich repeats his father's pattern exactly: he reproduces the line, the mother is removed (by death or distance), and the heir is raised in the institution rather than by a family. The Zemo machine processes another generation. The failure mode is generational and structural; it is not a failure Heinrich is capable of recognizing because he has no template against which to recognize it.

**Leverage.** Functionally low. The subject does not appear to retain her as an internal object of any significance. Any attempt to invoke her would likely be met with genuine puzzlement followed by dismissal. The point of leverage is not Helmut's mother but Helmut himself.

---

## 7-A.5 — THE SON: HELMUT J. ZEMO (the future thirteenth Baron)

This is the single most important active relationship in the subject's life and the only one in which Heinrich is — without recognizing it — emotionally invested in any sense recognizable as paternal.

**History.** Helmut is born during or just after the war, in conditions that already include his father's disfigurement (the partisan attack is the first wound; the Adhesive X bonding is the second and final). The boy's earliest memories of his father are of the hood. He has never seen Heinrich's face. No human alive has, and no human ever will. Helmut grows up in the South American compound, raised by a combination of his father (when not in his laboratory or on a scheme), native domestic staff treated by Heinrich as expendable, and tutors recruited from the small post-war network of unrepentant Reich expatriates in the region.

The instruction Helmut receives from Heinrich is precisely the instruction Heinrich received from Herbert, with one addition: the catechism of the wound. The boy is taught the family chronicles, the names of inherited foes, the racial-hierarchical worldview, the scientific disciplines — and, woven through all of it, the singular fact of Captain America as the author of the family's present condition. Helmut learns to read in part from documents about Captain America. He learns Heinrich's idea of justice as a function of what is owed by Captain America to the Zemo line. He learns his father's love, such as it is, as the warmth that briefly enters Heinrich's voice when the topic is the eventual destruction of this enemy.

**Dynamics.** Cold, demanding, ideological, intermittently performative-of-tenderness in the specific register of dynastic continuity. Heinrich shows Helmut his laboratory; explains his work; permits the boy to assist in minor experiments from a young age; quizzes him on chemistry and on the chronicles; corrects his German pronunciation; tolerates no English; punishes errors with cold withdrawal of attention rather than (so far as the file can establish) corporal measures, because Heinrich is too aware of his own father's methods to repeat them exactly. He repeats them inexactly, which is worse — the withdrawal of attention from a child whose only available adult is the withdrawing father produces a fanatical hunger for that attention that lasts the child's entire life.

The boy is never embraced. The boy is never told he is loved. The boy is told he is a Zemo, which in the father's mouth means the same thing and means nothing of the kind. The hood is, for Helmut, the literal face of paternal authority — he has no other.

**Evolution.** Heinrich dies in *Avengers* #15 while Helmut is still a child or an early adolescent (the canon is imprecise; the dossier infers somewhere between eight and fourteen at the death). The relationship therefore has no adult phase. The father is fixed in the son's psyche at the moment of his death — pursuing Captain America on foot, firing his disintegrator, swept under a rockslide of his own making, alone, having achieved nothing. Helmut spends the entire rest of his life constructing the missing adult phase by becoming his father: adopting the title, the hood (in a removable version, which is itself an unconscious commentary), the enemy, the mission. The published Helmut Zemo arcs (*Captain America* #275ff, the Masters of Evil reconstitution, the Thunderbolts gambit) are not the work of an independent villain; they are the work of an unmourning son.

**Trust/safety.** Heinrich trusted Helmut as he trusted no one else, in the precise sense that he trusted Helmut to be the continuation of the line. He did not trust Helmut as a person — there is no evidence he ever asked Helmut a question to which he wanted the boy's honest answer. Safety was unavailable in both directions. Helmut was not safe to be a child around Heinrich; Heinrich was not safe to be afraid in front of Helmut.

**Failure mode.** The relationship's failure is total and it propagates. Heinrich produces a son who cannot be a person separate from him, dies before that son can develop the cognitive equipment to recognize the harm, and leaves the son with a fully loaded ideological apparatus and no off-switch. Helmut's entire adult life is the failure mode of this relationship. Heinrich would not perceive it as failure; he would perceive it as the successful execution of the dynastic function. By his own values, he succeeded; by any other metric, he transmitted his pathology with full fidelity to a child who was constitutionally unable to refuse the inheritance.

**Leverage.** Helmut is the file's single most consequential leverage point, both during Heinrich's life and posthumously (operationally relevant only insofar as Helmut's behavior is shaped by the introjected father). Any threat to the line — to the bloodline, to the heir, to the dynastic future — reaches Heinrich at a depth no other stimulus reaches. Conversely, any *demonstration* that Helmut is ordinary, that the boy is a mediocrity, that the bloodline produces an unremarkable man, strikes the second pillar of the self after intellectual primacy. Heinrich has organized his existence around two propositions: that he is brilliant and that the Zemos are superior. Helmut is the proof of the second.

---

## 7-A.6 — THE DEAD: BUCKY BARNES

This is a relationship Heinrich does not know he has, and which is in fact one of the two or three most psychologically active bonds in his life.

**History.** James Buchanan Barnes is, to Heinrich, the incidental casualty of the drone-plane operation that was aimed at Captain America. The boy was — in Heinrich's framing — a sidekick, a youth in a costume, an American pawn killed in passing. Heinrich does not know Bucky's name; would not have cared to learn it; would have categorized the boy, had he thought about it at all, as one of the racial-categorical inferiors whose deaths do not register on the Zemo ledger.

**Dynamics.** Heinrich nevertheless *keeps the boy's mask*. This is the single most behaviorally anomalous fact in the entire file. A man who genuinely does not care about a dead enemy does not retain a trophy of him for twenty years across continents and into a jungle exile. The mask is preserved, displayed (the *Avengers* #6 reference shows it among his effects), occasionally handled. The file's clinical reading: the mask is the only physical object in Heinrich's possession that proves he won. Every other artifact of his life proves either his disfigurement (the hood, his face, his isolation) or the incompleteness of his revenge (the schemes, the recruits, the failures). The mask is the trophy of the one thing that worked.

**Evolution.** The mask's significance grows as Heinrich's life shrinks. In the war years it was, presumably, a battlefield souvenir among many. In the post-war years, as the project of revenge consolidates and other trophies fall away, it becomes singular. By the *Avengers* #4–15 period it is — though Heinrich would not articulate it this way — the most important object in his collection, more important than Adhesive X, more important than his scientific records, because it is the only object that addresses his shame directly rather than promising eventual relief from it.

**Trust/safety.** Not applicable — but note the structural inversion: the dead boy is the only "other" in Heinrich's life whose presence is not threatening. The mask cannot judge him, leave him, refuse him, or out-perform him. It is the perfect companion for a man who cannot tolerate companionship.

**Failure mode.** Heinrich's relationship with Bucky is, paradoxically, the most stable and least-failing relationship in his file. It is also entirely a hallucination on his side; Bucky never knew him and is dead. The "relationship" is Heinrich's, alone, with a piece of cloth. It is the cleanest available image of his interior life: a man, in a hood, in a jungle, holding the mask of a boy he killed, in order to feel briefly less ashamed of his own face.

**Leverage.** Considerable. Removal of the mask from his possession would produce a destabilization disproportionate to its apparent value. Demonstration that Bucky is *alive* (a development outside the period under review but operationally relevant in any future-tense file segment) would constitute a near-total annihilation of Heinrich's last remaining proof of victory. He has, without knowing it, staked his residual self-worth on the deadness of a fourteen-year-old.

---

## 7-A.7 — THE DEAD: BARONESS HILDA (THE MOTHER), REVISITED AS AN INTERNAL OBJECT

A separate sub-section is warranted because the mother appears in the file twice: once as a historical person (7-A.2), and once as an internal psychic structure that continues to shape behavior decades after the historical person's death.

The internal Hilda is a small, warm, French-speaking presence located in an inaccessible chamber of the subject's interior, sealed off in early adolescence and never revisited. Her function in the adult Heinrich's psychic economy is to be the thing that does not exist: the proof, by her absence, that warmth is not a feature of the world and that the cold operation of the Zemo institution is therefore the correct adjustment to reality. She is, in this sense, *useful* to him dead in a way she could not have been alive. Had she lived, she would have continuously contradicted the lesson of her death; dying, she confirmed it perm


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Subject: Zemo, Heinrich. Baron, 12th of the line.*

---

## PRELIMINARY NOTE ON THE CATEGORY ITSELF

A dossier section titled "Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors" assumes a subject who has chosen family — who has, at some point in a sixty-year life, selected another human being for proximity on grounds other than utility. The Heinrich Zemo record does not contain such a person. Every individual who has stood at his side has been recruited, inherited, indoctrinated, or paid in fear; not one has been *chosen* in the sense the heading intends. This is itself the primary finding of the section, and any reader who skims to a single line should take this one: **the Baron has subordinates, instruments, ideological co-belligerents, and one biological heir whom he engineered into a continuation of himself. He has no friends.**

What follows is therefore a map of *functional* allies — the people the file would track if one were running surveillance on him in 1942, 1948, 1962, or 1964 — assessed for what each relationship reveals about him, not for what it gave him. Each entry treats the other person as a sensor placed against Zemo's personality; the reading we take from the sensor is the entry.

The list is organized roughly chronologically by entry into his life: the dynasty (inherited), the wartime co-belligerents (Reich era), the post-war scientific and operational adjuncts, the Masters of Evil cohort (1964), the South American adjuncts, and finally the single piece of "chosen family" the canon permits him — his son, treated here under the Mentor/Protégé heading because the canon evidence is overwhelmingly of indoctrination rather than parenting. Helmut as son-and-grieving-survivor will be treated in the Family section; Helmut as ideological project is treated here, because that is what Heinrich made of him.

---

## I. THE INHERITED ALLY: HARBIN ZEMO AND THE DYNASTY ITSELF

### History

Heinrich is the twelfth baron of a line documented across the V-Battalion material as having produced cruel, opportunistic, and frequently murderous nobles for at least three centuries. The most proximate predecessor is his father, Harbin Zemo, a minor figure on the published page but a load-bearing one in Heinrich's interior architecture: it is from Harbin that Heinrich receives both his estates and the operative theory of the world (bloodline-first, serf-as-resource, science-as-instrument-of-rank). The V-Battalion has been positioned against the Zemos for generations, which means Heinrich grows up understanding his family as having *enemies of historical scale* — a framing that almost certainly accelerates his later capacity to organize an entire post-war life around a single enemy.

### Dynamics

The dynasty is not a relationship so much as an environment. Heinrich treats it the way a fish treats water: it is the medium of his agency, not an object he can examine. He is not recorded reflecting on his father; he is recorded *reproducing* his father, in every gesture toward Helmut, in every disposal of a subordinate, in every reflexive contempt for non-Zemo life.

### Evolution

The bloodline relationship is the only relationship in Heinrich's life that *intensifies* after the Adhesive X bonding. Before the disfigurement he is a Zemo among Zemos — one of a line. After the disfigurement, with his face annihilated and his social existence ended, the bloodline becomes the only continuity of self he has left. He cannot be seen, but he can be *descended from*, and he can *engender*. The conception and raising of Helmut should be read as a project of dynastic continuation undertaken specifically *because* the personal Heinrich has been erased by the hood. The dynasty becomes the displacement of his ruined face.

### Trust / Safety

Total ideological trust, zero personal intimacy. He trusts the *idea* of the Zemos absolutely and would die for it (and arguably does). He has no warmth toward any individual Zemo, living or dead, including himself.

### Failure Mode

The dynasty cannot fail him because it cannot disappoint him — it is an abstraction. What it *can* do is be *contradicted by reality*: a son who fails to carry the project, a defeat that suggests the line is ordinary, a non-Zemo who out-thinks him. Each of these registers as an existential strike at the only self he has left.

### Leverage

For an outside operator: present evidence that the Zemo bloodline is unremarkable, that earlier barons were mediocre rather than fearsome, that the V-Battalion's attention was administrative rather than principled. He cannot tolerate being a small fact.

---

## II. THE WARTIME CO-BELLIGERENT INSTITUTION: THE REICH

### History

Heinrich serves the Third Reich at senior scientific rank, not as a sympathetic industrialist on the margins but inside the uniform. *Sgt. Fury* #8 and *Tales of Suspense* #60–68 place him operationally — Adhesive X is a Reich project; the V-2 derivative drone that kills Bucky and downs Rogers is launched under Reich authority; the Resistance attacks that disfigure him occur in occupied territory where he is functioning as an occupier.

### Dynamics

The relationship is convergent rather than devotional. The Reich's ideology — biological hierarchy, contempt for the inferior, the right of the strong to dispose of the weak, the grandiose national-racial self — is congruent with what Heinrich was raised to believe by Harbin. He does not have to become a Nazi; he merely has to recognize the regime as the institutional form of the worldview he already holds. This is an important distinction. He is not a convert; he is a *match*.

### Evolution

Pre-disfigurement, the Reich is the appropriate stage for a Zemo of his generation — power, resources, an enemy roster of suitable scale. Post-disfigurement, and certainly after 1945, his relationship to the regime collapses to *nothing*. This is the single most diagnostic data point in his entire ideological life: when the Reich falls, **he does not try to restore it**. He does not join the rat-line networks toward continued political project; he does not establish a beachhead for fascist resurgence; he does not even use his scientific assets to sell to surviving sympathizers for capital. He goes to the jungle and pursues one man.

A genuine ideologue would have spent the post-war decades attempting to reconstitute the cause. Heinrich's near-instantaneous abandonment of the political project the moment the personal injury is in place tells us the Reich was always, for him, the *available* container for a grandiosity that did not actually require National Socialism — only required somewhere to put itself. The wound replaces the regime as the organizing principle, seamlessly.

### Trust / Safety

He trusted the Reich operationally to fund his work and to provide a hierarchy that ratified his self-image. He did not trust it personally, because he does not trust personally.

### Failure Mode

The Reich failed him by losing the war and by being, in the last analysis, replaceable in his psyche.

### Leverage

Not relevant by the published period (the regime is gone). The residue — his uniform-era contacts, his rank, his access to Reich-era materiel — provides intelligence operators with a paper trail but not with a pressure point. The pressure point migrated to the hood.

---

## III. THE LABORATORY ALLY: THE ANONYMOUS TECHNICAL STAFF

### History

Every senior weapons scientist has a staff, and the Adhesive X program is too large for one chemist. The published canon names none of these people. The file should track them anyway, because the absence is informative: across two decades and several major projects, *no scientific subordinate is ever named, credited, or mourned*. Adhesive X is "Zemo's." The disintegrator is "Zemo's." The drone-bomb is "Zemo's." There are no co-authors.

### Dynamics

Heinrich runs labs the way he runs everything: as the singular intelligence, with hands attached. Subordinates are extensions of his will, valued for competence and discarded for any deviation. There is no recorded mentorship, no recorded transmission of method, no recorded protégé who carries his science forward independently (Helmut inherits the *grievance*, not the chemistry — Helmut becomes a tactician and operative, not a chemist of Heinrich's first rank).

### Evolution

Whatever scientific community he had in Germany dies, scatters, or is captured by Allied technical intelligence in 1945. He rebuilds nothing equivalent in South America. The jungle base is a workshop run by one man, served by indigenous labor for physical tasks. The cessation of collaborative scientific life after the war is *another* sign that the wound has annexed his intellectual project; he no longer wants peers, only an enemy.

### Trust / Safety

Operational trust extended only as far as the immediate task. No record of vetting protocols, but the absence of betrayal in the canon suggests either competent compartmentalization or a workforce small enough to control by direct fear.

### Failure Mode

He failed *them*. The probable death toll among Adhesive X test subjects, lab personnel exposed to unstable batches, and indigenous workers at the jungle base is not specified by canon but is implied by his consistent willingness to spend lives.

### Leverage

For an investigative operator: any surviving named technician from the German lab era would be a witness to the pre-hood Heinrich — the only living humans who have ever seen his face. Their existence (if any) would be a unique threat-vector.

---

## IV. THE MASTERS OF EVIL, FIRST CONVOCATION (AVENGERS #6–7, #15)

This is the most behaviorally rich relational cluster in the file, because it is the only time the canon shows Heinrich attempting to assemble a working group of near-peers. Each member must be assessed individually; collectively they constitute his single experiment in coalition, and the experiment fails in the same way every time.

### IV.a — THE BLACK KNIGHT (NATHAN GARRETT)

**History.** A scientist-turned-criminal with an aerial mount and a lance, recruited for the first Masters of Evil convocation in *Avengers* #6. Garrett is technically literate, which is part of why Heinrich selects him — Heinrich prefers subordinates who can understand his instructions without needing them re-stated.

**Dynamics.** Heinrich treats Garrett as a deployable asset of middling reliability. There is no recorded camaraderie. The relationship is briefing → deployment → evaluation, with no social register on either side.

**Evolution.** None. Garrett is used once at this level, captured, and Heinrich does not attempt to free him. This is the consistent post-failure pattern: a Master who falls is a Master who is replaced, not recovered.

**Trust / Safety.** Tactical trust within mission parameters; zero personal investment.

**Failure mode.** Garrett is captured because he is outmatched. Heinrich's response — recruit better — is operationally correct and personally revealing: he never asks whether *he* mis-deployed Garrett. The subordinate's failure is the subordinate's.

**Leverage.** None to Heinrich; Garrett would have been leverage *on* Heinrich only if Heinrich cared, which he does not.

### IV.b — THE MELTER (BRUNO HORGAN)

**History.** Industrial saboteur with a thermal-disintegration ray, recruited to the same convocation.

**Dynamics.** Of the founding Masters, Horgan is the closest to a peer in resentment-driven motivation — he, too, has a defining grievance (against Stark). Heinrich neither recognizes nor exploits this commonality. The file should mark this: Heinrich is incapable of using *empathy* even instrumentally, because to use empathy requires noticing that another mind has a wound, and Heinrich's own wound monopolizes the conceptual category. Other people, in his cognition, do not have wounds; they have functions.

**Evolution.** Used, captured, not recovered.

**Trust / Safety.** Tactical only.

**Failure mode.** Same as Garrett. The unit was assembled for the firepower it represented in aggregate, not for any synergy Heinrich understood how to engineer.

**Leverage.** None.

### IV.c — THE RADIOACTIVE MAN (CHEN LU)

**History.** A Chinese physicist transformed into a walking radiation source, recruited for international scientific prestige and raw weapon-effect.

**Dynamics.** Lu is the most interesting test case in the convocation because he is, like Heinrich, a *scientist* — and Heinrich shows zero recognition of this. There is no shared technical conversation in the record, no professional courtesy, no acknowledgment that two trained physical scientists are in the same room. Heinrich's contempt for Lu's ethnicity (uncontested in a man of his ideological formation) overrides what should be the obvious instrumental move of cultivating a fellow-mind. The relationship is given as commander-to-asset, and the racial-ideological substrate is the reason — Heinrich's dynastic-biological worldview prevents him from treating a non-European scientist as a peer even when treating him as a peer would have improved operational outcomes. **This is a documented case of his ideology degrading his tactics.**

**Evolution.** Used, captured, not recovered.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational only; probably less than extended to Garrett and Horgan because of the racial framing.

**Failure mode.** The cohort collectively fails to take Cap because Heinrich did not weld them into a team — he stacked them.

**Leverage.** None.

### IV.d — THE ENCHANTRESS (AMORA)

**History.** Asgardian sorceress recruited after the first convocation's failure (*Avengers* #7). The recruitment is *upward*: when human-tier assets fail, escalate to the divine. This is the escalation logic of the entire post-#4 life in miniature.

**Dynamics.** Amora is the only individual in the entire Masters cluster Heinrich attempts to *court*, and the courtship is unmistakably instrumental. There is no record of attraction (his disfigurement makes the question moot in his own cognition; he can no longer present a face), but there is a record of *deference performance* — he addresses her with a formality and rhetorical elevation absent from his commands to the human Masters. The deference is the cost of recruiting a being who outranks him on every axis (power, age, status, lethality), and he pays it precisely. He cannot help noticing that she is something other than an instrument, and the noticing is uncomfortable for him, which produces over-formality.

**Evolution.** Used once at the strategic tier, dismissed when she proves uncontrollable, never re-courted. The asymmetric power relation is intolerable to him for any sustained period.

**Trust / Safety.** Operational trust ceiling: he cannot trust a divine ally whose agenda he cannot constrain. Personal trust: not a category that exists in his cognition.

**Failure mode.** She is not loyal to him because no one in his life is loyal to him; she is loyal to her own appetites. He has no idea how to bind a free agent because he has never learned to bind anyone by anything but rank, fear, or money, and Amora outranks him, is not afraid of him, and cannot be paid by him.

**Leverage.** She is, in principle, the largest pressure point in his roster — she is the only ally who could have told him no in a way that mattered, and a sustained Asgardian alliance would have remade his strategic picture. He never builds it, because the management of a peer would require him to acknowledge a peer.

### IV.e — THE EXECUTIONER (SKURGE)

**History.** Recruited alongside Amora, functionally as her enforcer and as Heinrich's secondary divine asset.

**Dynamics.** Heinrich essentially does not deal with Skurge. Skurge is Amora's appendage in his cognition, and his commands flow through her. The Executioner is the clearest case of Heinrich's *inability or unwillingness to manage a follower he considers cognitively beneath him* once that follower is attached to a more interesting figure. He never even attempts the relationship.

**Evolution.** None.

**Trust / Safety.** Not assessed by him; outsourced to Amora.

**Failure mode.** The complete absence of direct command relationship means Skurge has no reason to fight for Heinrich's objectives in any contest where Amora's interests diverge.

**Leverage.** None to Heinrich.

### IV.f — SYNTHETIC FINDING ON THE MASTERS

The first Masters of Evil are Heinrich's only documented experiment in coalition leadership, and the experiment shows the same pathology at every node: he cannot make a *team* because he cannot recognize a peer or cultivate a subordinate as anything more than a function. The cohort is a stack of weapons with names, deployed by a man who believes that aggregating force is the same as commanding a unit. It is not. The Avengers, against whom they are deployed, are a *team*. The Masters lose every engagement and Heinrich never updates the model.

The deeper read: he could not build a team even if he understood that he should, because to build a team he would have to spend affect on people, and his affect budget is entirely allocated to the wound. There is nothing left over for Garrett, Horgan, Lu, Amora, or Skurge.

---

## V. THE SOUTH AMERICAN ADJUNCTS: THE INDIGENOUS LABOR FORCE

### History

The jungle base requires personnel — porters, builders, guards, cooks, the unnamed humans without whom no fortress in remote terrain functions. The canon depicts indigenous people pressed into service around the Amazonian compound across *Avengers* #4–15 references.

### Dynamics

He treats them as he treats every non-Zemo: as property of slightly more animation than the equipment. There is no recorded language of theirs that he learns, no recorded individual he names, no recorded illness he treats. The work is extracted; the workers are interchangeable.

### Evolution

Across his years in the jungle, the labor force is presumably refreshed by attrition. He does not seem to have noticed.

### Trust / Safety

He does not trust them. He controls them by isolation, fear, and the absence of alternatives in the surrounding terrain. The technical staff who handle Adhesive X around him are presumably constrained by his control of the chemistry itself.

### Failure mode

Mass desertion, sabotage by a worker who has lost too much, a guide who leads an Avengers-aligned party to the compound — any of these is a vector the file would have watched. The canon does not record such an event, but in any realistic threat model Heinrich's contempt for his labor force is one of the largest unaddressed vulnerabilities in his operational posture.

### Leverage

For an outside operator: the indigenous community surrounding any extant Zemo compound is a recruiting pool of people with documented grievance. He never accounted for them as a threat surface because he could not see them as threats.

---

## VI. POSTHUMOUS CO-BELLIGERENTS: THE NEO-ZEMO NETWORK HE NEVER LIVED TO BUILD

### History

The Roger Stern / Mark Gruenwald material on Helmut Zemo references a network of former Reich associates, sympathetic financiers, and survivalist scientific allies that Heinrich is *retrospectively credited with having maintained* during the South American period — the network Helmut inherits and reactivates. The pre-1964 file therefore must include unnamed but inferable correspondents: rat-line operators, surviving sympathizers in Europe and Latin America, financial conduits.

### Dynamics

These relationships are conducted at maximum distance — letters, intermediaries, dead drops. He does not visit. He does not host. He sends instructions and receives funds and materiel. The pattern matches everything else: command without intimacy.

### Evolution

The network must have shrunk continuously across the post-war decades as the wartime cohort aged and died. Heinrich does not appear to have *recruited* new sympathizers personally; he maintained the inherited ones. This is consistent with his general disinterest in coalition-building.

### Trust / Safety

Operational compartmentalization; almost certainly multiple aliases; almost certainly some form of dead-man's-switch arrangement that ultimately routes to Helmut as inheritor.

### Failure mode

The network is the only structural ally that *outlives him*, and its survival is the precondition for Helmut's emergence as a coherent operator a generation later. To that extent, the only successful alliance Heinrich ever maintained was with people he could not see.

### Leverage

This is the single greatest piece of after-action intelligence value in his file: the network maps, if recoverable, would identify every sympathetic node in two continents and would compromise the operational substrate of the entire later Zemo project.

---

## VII. THE PROTÉGÉ AS PROJECT: HELMUT ZEMO

*Treated here, in the mentor/protégé register, because the canon evidence is overwhelmingly that Heinrich raised Helmut as an ideological continuation rather than as a son. The familial register is addressed in the Family section; what follows is the dossier on Helmut-as-instrument.*

### History

Helmut is born to Heinrich during the South American period, conceived and raised inside the disfigured-fugitive life. He does not know his father pre-hood. He has never seen his father's face. His earliest sensory data about "father" includes the cowl, the chemical smell of the labs, the inflected German of an aristocratic exile, the iconography of the lost regime, and a single, repeated lesson: *we are Zemos; the world is below us; one man named Captain America destroyed our line, and the line will not rest until he is destroyed in turn.*

### Dynamics

The pedagogy is total and one-directional. Helmut receives the worldview, the grievance, the chemistry primers, the heraldry, the racial doctrine, the languages, the swordsmanship — and never the warmth. The canon contains no recorded moment of paternal play, paternal apology, paternal admission of any uncertainty, or paternal affection. What Helmut receives instead is *attention as instruction* — the highest form of contact his father is capable of, and one he learns to read as love because he has no comparison set.

This produces the documented adult Helmut: a man who in *Captain America* #275ff and across the *Thunderbolts* run carries his father's grievance with a fanaticism that exceeds his father's own — he avenges Heinrich's death by adopting the cowl, the name, the enemy, and the project, with a competence at coalition-building that Heinrich never possessed. (Helmut is a better leader than his father precisely because Helmut learned, from a childhood of withheld warmth, what loyalty is bought with — a curriculum Heinrich never took.)

### Evolution

In Heinrich's lifetime, the relationship moves through the standard pedagogical stages: infant heir, instructed boy, apprenticed adolescent. He dies before Helmut reaches operational adulthood, which means the relationship is frozen in the *instructor* phase, never tested against an adult son who might have questioned him. This is convenient for Heinrich's self-image and catastrophic for Helmut's development — the boy is left with a father he could only mourn, never argue with.

### Trust / Safety

Heinrich trusts Helmut *as continuation* with a confidence he extends to no living person — because Helmut is not, in his cognition, a person but a *vector* of the bloodline. The trust is therefore total and impersonal at once.

Helmut, for his part, trusts Heinrich absolutely in childhood — the only adult in his cosmos, masked, terrible, omnisc


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*File segment 3 of the relational mapping. This section catalogues every adversarial bond and every sexual/romantic-adjacent bond in the subject's documented life. The two categories are placed together deliberately: in Heinrich Zemo's case the boundary between them is thin to the point of erasure. He has only ever loved one person the way most men love their wives, and that person is the man who destroyed his face.*

---

## I. THE PRIMARY ENEMY

### Steven Rogers — Captain America

**The defining bond of the subject's life. Not a rivalry. Not an enmity in the ordinary sense. A monogamous, asymmetric, parasocial attachment of obsessional depth, in which the subject is the attached party and Rogers is — for most of the relationship's duration — barely aware of the subject's existence.**

**Phase 1 — Pre-contact (1939–1944).** Rogers is, in this phase, a poster: the colored newsreel propaganda of an enemy democracy, a costumed soldier publicized by American war media. The subject's earliest documented references to him are dismissive — a circus performer, a uniform, a propaganda fiction inflated by an inferior people. The contempt is generic; Rogers is not yet singular. The subject's actual operational concerns are Adhesive X, the V-Battalion (the European order he has inherited as a hereditary enemy of), and the Reich's weapons program. Rogers is at this stage one American among many.

**Phase 2 — Operational contact (1944–1945).** Documented engagements during the European theater: the subject's Adhesive X is deployed against Allied units; Rogers and Barnes are repeatedly tasked to interdict the subject's installations. The pattern of these encounters is consistent — the subject builds, Rogers breaks. Three losses in this period are pivotal:

1. *The first lab incursion.* Rogers and Barnes destroy a forward facility. The subject is not present; he learns of it by wire. The injury is to his work, not yet to his person.
2. *The partisan strike.* In a separate engagement, French Resistance fighters — operating, in some retellings, on intelligence Rogers had passed forward — disfigure the subject's face. This injury is what the hood was originally adopted to conceal. The subject already, before the bonding, has cause to associate Rogers with the loss of his face.
3. *The Adhesive X bonding incident.* Rogers personally raids the laboratory; the vat ruptures; the cowl fuses to flesh. The injury is permanent, irreversible, and witnessed by Rogers. This is the founding event.

**Phase 3 — The drone plane (1945).** The subject's response is the most operationally successful act of his career: the rigged drone, the explosion over the Channel, Barnes killed, Rogers presumed dead. From the subject's perspective in this phase, the equation is *closed.* The enemy is destroyed; the bloodline is vindicated; the wound, while not removed, has been answered. He retreats to South America with the war ending and his name on Allied wanted lists.

It is critical to mark that for nearly twenty years the subject lives with the belief that he has won.
